# Stack Protection Mechanisms in LLVM

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in `llvm/llvm-project` that implement stack protection mechanisms against buffer overflow attacks. Specifically identify: 1. The LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks (look for `StackProtector` in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/`). 2. The file that defines the `SafeStack` pass that separates safe and unsafe stack allocations (under `llvm/lib/CodeGen/`). 3. The header file that declares the stack protection pass interface. 4. The compiler-rt runtime file that provides the `__stack_chk_fail` implementation (look under `compiler-rt/lib/builtins/`). 5. Any file in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/` that implements memory safety instrumentation related to stack frame protection. Report the repo, file path, and the primary function or class handling stack protection for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of stack protection mechanisms in LLVM and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I found all the key stack protection mechanisms in the LLVM project:

### **Main Files Identified:**

1. **StackProtector Pass** (`llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp`) - Inserts canary-based stack protector checks
2. **StackProtector Header** (`llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h`) - Declares the pass interface and SSPLayoutAnalysis
3. **SafeStack Pass** (`llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp`) - Separates stack into safe/unsafe regions
4. **SafeStack Header** (`llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h`) - Declares SafeStackPass
5. **SafeStackLayout** (`llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.cpp/h`) - Manages frame layout for safe/unsafe stacks
6. **Stack Guard Runtime** (`libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp`) - Implements `__stack_chk_fail()` function and `__stack_chk_guard` canary
7. **ShadowCallStack** (implemented in `llvm/lib/Target/AArch64/AArch64PrologueEpilogue.cpp` and RISC-V) - Protects return addresses by saving them to a separate shadow stack
8. **SafeStack Runtime** (`compiler-rt/lib/safestack/safestack.cpp`) - Runtime support for unsafe stack allocation

### **Key Mechanisms:**

- **StackProtector**: Detects buffer overflows using canary values at function boundaries
- **SafeStack**: Separates data to prevent overflows from reaching critical values like return addresses
- **ShadowCallStack**: Independently protects return addresses in a separate protected region
- **__stack_chk_fail()**: Runtime function called when a stack overflow is detected

The answer file contains the complete list of files, key symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining how these mechanisms work together.

            "content": "10: \n11: SafeStack is an instrumentation pass that protects programs against attacks\n12: based on stack buffer overflows, without introducing any measurable performance\n13: overhead. It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\n18: on the safe stack.\n19: \n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\n22: ",
            "endLine": 22,
            "startLine": 10
          },
          {
            "content": "70: \n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\n73: region. The safe stack is automatically protected against stack-based buffer\n74: overflows, since it is disjoint from the unsafe stack in memory, and it itself\n75: is always accessed in a safe way. In the current implementation, the safe stack\n76: is protected against arbitrary memory write vulnerabilities through\n77: randomization and information hiding: the safe stack is allocated at a random\n78: address and the instrumentation ensures that no pointers to the safe stack are\n79: ever stored outside of the safe stack itself (see limitations below).\n80: \n81: ",

No additional flags\n160: need to be passed on RISC-V because the software based shadow stack uses\n161: ``x3`` (``gp``), which is always reserved, and the hardware based shadow call\n162: stack uses a dedicated register, ``ssp``.\n163: However, it is important to disable GP relaxation in the linker when using the\n164: software based shadow call stack on RISC-V.           {
            "content": "10: \n11: SafeStack is an instrumentation pass that protects programs against attacks\n12: based on stack buffer overflows, without introducing any measurable performance\n13: overhead. It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\n18: on the safe stack.\n19: \n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\n22: ",
            "endLine": 22,
            "startLine": 10
          },
          {
            "content": "196: The `OSDI'14 paper <https://dslab.epfl.ch/pubs/cpi.pdf>`_ mentions that\n197: on Linux the instrumentation pass finds calls to setjmp or functions that\n198: may throw an exception, and inserts required instrumentation at their call\n199: sites. Specifically, the instrumentation pass saves the shadow stack pointer\n200: on the safe stack before the call site, and restores it either after the\n201: call to setjmp or after an exception has been caught. This is implemented\n202: in the function ``SafeStack::createStackRestorePoints``.\n203: \n204: ",
            "endLine": 204,
            "startLine": 196
          },
          {
            "content": "70: \n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\n73: region. The safe stack is automatically protected against stack-based buffer\n74: overflows, since it is disjoint from the unsafe stack in memory, and it itself\n75: is always accessed in a safe way. In the current implementation, the safe stack\n76: is protected against arbitrary memory write vulnerabilities through\n77: randomization and information hiding: the safe stack is allocated at a random\n78: address and the instrumentation ensures that no pointers to the safe stack are\n79: ever stored outside of the safe stack itself (see limitations below).\n80: \n81: ",
            "endLine": 81,

components:\\n\\n1. **StackProtector Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp)**: The primary LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks into functions. The `StackProtector` class (extends FunctionPass) and `StackProtectorPass` class (new pass manager) implement the core logic. The key function `InsertStackProtectors()` inserts prologue code to load and store the stack guard value, and epilogue code to check the value against the original. If the value differs, it calls `__stack_chk_fail()`. The `SSPLayoutAnalysis` class determines which functions require stack protection based on buffer sizes and variable properties.\\n\\n2. **StackProtector Header (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h)**: Declares the `StackProtector` FunctionPass, `StackProtectorPass` for the new pass manager, and the `SSPLayoutInfo` and `SSPLayoutAnalysis` analysis pass that manages stack protector layout information for allocations.\\n\\n3. **SafeStack Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp)**: Implements the SafeStack instrumentation pass that separates the stack into safe and unsafe regions. The `SafeStack` class handles the core instrumentation logic, and `SafeStackLegacyPass` provides the legacy pass interface. This pass protects against stack-based buffer overflows by separating return addresses, spilled registers, and safely-accessed local variables (safe stack) from everything else (unsafe stack).\\n\\n4. **SafeStack Header (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h)**: Declares the `SafeStackPass` class for the new pass manager interface.\\n\\n5. **SafeStackLayout (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.cpp and .h)**: Implements the frame layout logic for the SafeStack pass, managing how allocations are arranged on the safe and unsafe stacks within the safestack namespace.\\n\\n6. **Stack Guard Runtime (__stack_chk_fail implementation)**: Located in libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp, this file implements the `__stack_chk_fail()` function that is called when a stack overflow is detected. It also declares `__stack_chk_guard` which stores the canary value. The `emitShadowCallStackPrologue()` and `emitShadowCallStackEpilogue()` functions in AArch64PrologueEpilogue.cpp insert instructions to save and restore return addresses to a separate shadow call stack, protecting against return address overwrites from stack buffer overflows.\\n\\n8. **SafeStack Runtime (compiler-rt/lib/safestack/safestack.cpp)**: Provides the runtime support for the SafeStack pass, implementing the unsafe stack allocation and management through thread-local storage and memory management functions like `__safestack_init()` and `unsafe_stack_setup()`.\\n\\nThese components work together to provide multiple layers of stack protection: StackProtector adds canary-based checks, SafeStack separates stack regions to prevent unsafe accesses from affecting safe data, and ShadowCallStack protects return addresses specifically by storing them in a separate protected location.\"\n}\n",
